<div id="review_186563062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/186563062" />
    <a title="Lee Ellen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5570286-lee-ellen"><img alt="Lee Ellen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308102756p2/5570286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/186563062?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee Ellen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee Ellen" href="/user/show/5570286-lee-ellen">Lee Ellen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186563062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15951913144745502630">This was a fun 300 page book. Unfortunately, it continued for an additional 200 pages. Like "Night Watch," "Day Watch" introduces us to magicians, shape-shifters, and vampires that must mind the crossing of t's and dotting of i's in magical law in order to keep a treaty between the powers of light and dark so that a conflagration at best or apocalypse at worst can be avoided. There is always a way around pro forma, however, and the plot derives from the loopholes found, alternately, by the light</span>
  <span id="freeText15951913144745502630" style="display:none">This was a fun 300 page book. Unfortunately, it continued for an additional 200 pages. Like "Night Watch," "Day Watch" introduces us to magicians, shape-shifters, and vampires that must mind the crossing of t's and dotting of i's in magical law in order to keep a treaty between the powers of light and dark so that a conflagration at best or apocalypse at worst can be avoided. There is always a way around pro forma, however, and the plot derives from the loopholes found, alternately, by the light and dark powers. Bored yet? Add another 100 pages of "if-then" scenarios by various magicians, and you have simulated the experience of reading this book. Sure, the constant subterfuge can lend itself to interesting moments, but it begins to feel too much like a free plot card as the novel drags on. At the end, I found myself exclaiming "Why not?!" instead of "Deus ex machina!" A credit is due to the author for finding his device. It has its moments: the social commentary directly relating to modern Russia, such as notes on idealistic young people with guitars, the nature of conversation with and without vodka, or the overzealous obnoxiousness of well-meaning do-gooders, made me laugh out loud or, at least, find a sympathetic soul to appreciate the lines. This is a fine book for mindless entertainment reading, although it is slightly less satisfying than Night Watch, which you will want to read first anyway. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15951913144745502630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81265112" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81265112" />
    <a title="Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/634946-daniel"><img alt="Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228517925p2/634946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81265112?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/634946-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/634946-daniel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81265112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17448164527922795981">As with the previous installation from this series, I enjoyed the complexity of the novels. They are chess games within chess games mixing history, politics, social engineering, mythology, and all sorts of other good things.<br/><br/>The second story of the three was a little long and drawn out, but everything comes together. I did have some fun trying to figure out who Vitaly was.<br/><br/>Lukyanenko continues his meditation on the nature of "good" and "evil" through the détante of the Watches as overseen by the I</span>
  <span id="freeText17448164527922795981" style="display:none">As with the previous installation from this series, I enjoyed the complexity of the novels. They are chess games within chess games mixing history, politics, social engineering, mythology, and all sorts of other good things.<br /><br />The second story of the three was a little long and drawn out, but everything comes together. I did have some fun trying to figure out who Vitaly was.<br /><br />Lukyanenko continues his meditation on the nature of "good" and "evil" through the détante of the Watches as overseen by the Inquisition. Despite the Treaty that keeps the Others from overrunning the mortal world with their conflict and "protecting" it from undue tampering, both sides are trying to win without breaking the rules. They will bend them to the point of breaking, but no breaking unless it's the endgame, I suppose.<br /><br />This was nominally a novel from the point of view of the Dark Ones, as <i>Night Watch</i> was a novel from the point of view of the Light Ones, but there was liberal use of Light One point of view. Anton Gorodetsky is still the protagonist in general, though the first story about Alisa Donnikova was very moving. She was an unrepentant Dark Witch, but she knew who she was and she knew how to love.<br /><br />I can't wait to read the next one and I hope the continue with the films as well, even though they change quite a bit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17448164527922795981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_11796232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/11796232" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/266227-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595789246p2/266227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11796232?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/266227-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone interested in a Russian take on the epic battle between good and evil </span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jennifer by: </span>
      the movie, Nightwatch
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11796232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13715066095208383250">In this interesting sequel to the book, Nightwatch, the epic battle between light and dark has a curious sort of beaurocracy to it. Sergei Lukyanenko creates a world where the forces of Light and Darkness have spent the last millenium in an uneasy stalemate--the balance of power maintained by a treaty and a group called the Inquisition.<br/><br/>Yet, the forces of Light and Dark are not so different--both are composed of "Others," supernatural beings who begin as human but must choose which side to belong</span>
  <span id="freeText13715066095208383250" style="display:none">In this interesting sequel to the book, Nightwatch, the epic battle between light and dark has a curious sort of beaurocracy to it. Sergei Lukyanenko creates a world where the forces of Light and Darkness have spent the last millenium in an uneasy stalemate--the balance of power maintained by a treaty and a group called the Inquisition.<br /><br />Yet, the forces of Light and Dark are not so different--both are composed of "Others," supernatural beings who begin as human but must choose which side to belong to. The forces of Light, the Nightwatch, monitor the forces of Dark while the forces of Dark, the Daywatch, do the same. <br /><br />This novel is divided into three separate but related stories. In the first, a young witch from the Dark falls in love with a magician from the Light. In the second, a powerful stranger comes to Moscow and seems to upset the balance of power between the Dark and the Light. In the third, a trial is held in Prague and both a Light Magician and a Dark one begin to suspect that their superiors are up to something. <br /><br />Though I liked the way all the parts of this novel eventually come together, the ending felt a little rushed as it set some of the characters up for the next book that is clearly to come.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13715066095208383250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_647633345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/647633345" />
    <a title="AmbWitch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12748335-ambwitch"><img alt="AmbWitch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547232553p2/12748335.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/647633345?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AmbWitch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AmbWitch" href="/user/show/12748335-ambwitch">AmbWitch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780099489931" href="/book/show/1108497.The_Day_Watch">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer647633345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11306914098819906686">Just like the last book in this series, I really enjoyed <i>Day Watch</i>, although not as much as <i>Night Watch</i>. As per usual, I’ve have left it a bit late to review this and have forgotten a lot of what goes on, or my ideas of the book, but here goes. <br/><br/><br/> In this book there are three separate stories that at first don’t seem to connect, until you get to the last one and the pieces start to fall into place. Then you realise that some of the events of the first two stories are manipulated and used to create</span>
  <span id="freeText11306914098819906686" style="display:none">Just like the last book in this series, I really enjoyed <i>Day Watch</i>, although not as much as <i>Night Watch</i>. As per usual, I’ve have left it a bit late to review this and have forgotten a lot of what goes on, or my ideas of the book, but here goes. <br /><br /><br /> In this book there are three separate stories that at first don’t seem to connect, until you get to the last one and the pieces start to fall into place. Then you realise that some of the events of the first two stories are manipulated and used to create the outcome of the third. <br /><br /><br /> Each story is told from a different perspective and although I prefer Anton’s, it was interesting to see things from a different point of view, especially from those of ‘dark’ characters. We were able to see that there’s not really that many differences between the two sides and how they were all being treated like pawns by their bosses.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I especially enjoyed the scene where a character from either side sit down and have a meal Liked seeing how people of both sides can have a meal together and in general get on with each other. They were both trying to get information from each other, but they also seemed to be getting along, like Alisa and Igor were able to get along until they found out what they both were. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /> At first I didn’t like Alisa and wasn’t particularly enjoying the book, but this could just have been because she wasn’t Anton. After a while she started to grow on me and I started to enjoy the book more. Towards the end of her story I even started to feel sorry for her and, a little annoyed. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I wasn’t too sure on Alisa’s death. I’d just started getting into her story and then she’s killed off. She died, because she didn’t want to kill the one she loved. What I found interesting here, was that if she hadn’t been in love with him, she may have had no problem in killing him and this sort of showed that her keeping him alive would have been for her own benefit, where as he killed her for the benefit of the light (or did he). If that made any sense at all. What I wanted to see was them defying the side they were on and being together, but that would be doing something for themselves and not their cause/people, which is more a trait of the dark than the light. <br /><br /><br /> Although they both had different ways of getting the energy from the kids, I didn’t really think Igor’s way was any better that Alisa’s. They both seemed to look after the kids they were in charge of but Igor left his feeling drained at times (I can’t remember whether Alisa did as well), and I didn’t really see this as a good thing. But then again, long back in this series you establish that the light ones do bad things to reach their overall goals.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /> I wasn’t that bothered about the middle story until towards the end where things started to add up. The main character of this one just held no interest for me. Yes, I wanted to know where he’d come from, and there was a lot of mystery behind this, but I had no interest in the actual character other than when he was interacting with others. <br /><br /><br /> I was glad to see Anton back, I much prefer his perspective and love the fact that he is a small character who’s always being used but that ends up having a huge impact. He spends so much time trying to find the reasons behind what is going on and trying to work out others intentions, while fighting the system and trying not to play right into the bosses hands. <br /><br /><br /> This series is becoming one of my favourites, as it seems to have an interesting way of looking at things. I will definitely be reading the next one, although it will be a while as I’ve made a deal with myself that I’m only allowed to buy a book for every ten I get rid of (it will be hard but I have way too many books).<br /><br /><br />P.S Did I read somewhere in here that Rammstein where werewolves or did I imagine that?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11306914098819906686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_5828705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5828705" />
    <a title="Dale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/329383-dale"><img alt="Dale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448977473p2/329383.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5828705?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dale" href="/user/show/329383-dale">Dale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5828705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13169246157505095991">This is the twenty-first book I read on my commute, and back to the genre well I go. A strange and wondrous sub-area of genre which I like to call "modern foreign urban magical horror."<br/><br/>Day Watch is actually the second book in a trilogy (I read the first book, Night Watch, some time ago in the Pre-Commute days) about the agencies of the supernatural in Russia in the present day. (The author is Russian and the novels are translated into English.) Basic Premise of the Trilogy #1: powerful supernatu</span>
  <span id="freeText13169246157505095991" style="display:none">This is the twenty-first book I read on my commute, and back to the genre well I go. A strange and wondrous sub-area of genre which I like to call "modern foreign urban magical horror."<br /><br />Day Watch is actually the second book in a trilogy (I read the first book, Night Watch, some time ago in the Pre-Commute days) about the agencies of the supernatural in Russia in the present day. (The author is Russian and the novels are translated into English.) Basic Premise of the Trilogy #1: powerful supernatural forces have always existed alongside humanity, in the form of Others - vampires, werewolves, witches, demons, etc. Basic Premise of the Trilogy #2: there are Light Others (benign shapeshifters, good witches and wizards) and Dark Others (vampires, evil magicians, demons) and the Light and the Dark have been at war since the dawn of time. Basic Premise of the Trilogy #3: millennia of outright warfare took such a toll on both the Light and the Dark that they came to a truce, and creating a system of checks and balances so that neither side can become too powerful. Basic Premise of the Trilogy #4: the two factions co-exist uneasily, and open warfare has been replaced by Machiavellian maneuvering on both sides, with Light and Dark angling to exploit loopholes in the treaty in order to become so powerful that the treaty becomes moot, as either Light will finally vanquish Dark completely, or Dark will utterly consume Light. In the mean time, the Others who work for the Watches on either side are usually only pawns in games played by their superiors.<br /><br />I love this trilogy (so far - plan on picking up the third book soon!) because it's so different from other things I've read. Even through the filter of supernatural characters and plots, the insight into life in Russia, with its decaying infrastructure and institutional corruption, is fascinating. The characters are all interesting, as well - the first book focuses on several Light Others, but Day Watch is all about the so-called evil Dark Others who are even more intriguing. (Day Watch are the "bad guys", keeping watch on the creatures of light who belong to the day; the Night Watch keeps watch on the creatures of darkness, so they are the "good guys".) The idea of reducing the struggle between Good and Evil to a chess game of deceit, power grabs, political feints and other such bureaucratic moves also amuses me greatly, as does the world-building, the imaginative natural laws that govern the powers of the supernatural creatures.<br /><br />It's one of the more absorbing and exotic worlds in genre fiction, and I'll be sad to see it go when I finish the third and final book. Definitely worth a look if you ever wondered what a government-oversight war between Good and Evil in a post-reform Iron Curtain society would look like. (And if you've never wondered that before, well, I bet you do now.)<br /><br /><br />Running total for types of books read on the commute:<br /><br />Classics: 1<br />Modern Lit: 4<br />Fantasy/sci-fi: 11<br />Non-fiction: 4<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13169246157505095991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237320732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237320732" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6946107-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483280158p2/6946107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237320732?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/6946107-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780434014439" href="/book/show/832359.The_Day_Watch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=better-than-chocolate">better-than-chocolate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=fantasy-aficionados-top-100">fantasy-aficionados-top-100</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=fantasy-it-s-a-kind-of-magic">fantasy-it-s-a-kind-of-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=fantasy-with-fangs">fantasy-with-fangs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=fantasy-with-fur">fantasy-with-fur</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6946107-sam?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237320732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9255346442295218327">As with the first book in the series (sorry, at this point I can't think of it as a trilogy any longer, since there's now six of them), this is three interwoven novellas forming a single longer book. Also as with the first, Andrew Bromfield seems to have done an excellent job of translating, there's so much subtlety and nuance here.<br/><br/>So, the stories: first up is Alisa, witch of the Day Watch. She turned up as a minor character in <i>The Night Watch</i>. Here she loses her magical ability after a battle w</span>
  <span id="freeText9255346442295218327" style="display:none">As with the first book in the series (sorry, at this point I can't think of it as a trilogy any longer, since there's now six of them), this is three interwoven novellas forming a single longer book. Also as with the first, Andrew Bromfield seems to have done an excellent job of translating, there's so much subtlety and nuance here.<br /><br />So, the stories: first up is Alisa, witch of the Day Watch. She turned up as a minor character in <i>The Night Watch</i>. Here she loses her magical ability after a battle with the Light, and is sent to a Pioneer Camp for Russian youngsters to recover—she can draw energy from the children and gradually rebuild her power. But then she meets another counsellor, Igor, and lust ensues. The second story is about Vitaly. Initially he has no memory of who he is or what he is, but throughout he learns more and increases in power until he's at a point where even Gesar and Zabulon are likely to have difficulty handling him. The third story is about Edgar, a magician with the Moscow Day Watch. He is sent to investigate in the aftermath of events in the first and second story, and comes to realise that he's being set up.<br /><br />Although you would expect that this book would be almost entirely about the Day Watch (as the first book was almost entirely about the Night Watch), in fact the Light Others play a fairly significant role here, and so there's maybe not as much Day Watchiness about it as I'd hoped. There are several leaps between first person and third person POV which can sometimes cause a bit of a jolt while you're reading. But I still loved it—even though one of the most intriguing characters for me (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tiger Cub <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) was killed in a very abrupt and distressing way. I think I was probably more sad about that than about anything else that took place. The third part was fairly introspective in places, and could be heavy going if you're not deeply involved in the story by that point.<br /><br />Alisa was pretty unlikeable and self-obsessed as a character. Vitaly veered between bewildered and omniscient. Edgar was probably the most likeable of the three leads. It was great to have Anton, Gesar and Zabulon make an appearance, and their characters grew during the course of the book. There's still the wonderful 'differentness' I enjoyed so much in the first book, and the story was moved along in the course of events, although the religious overtones of the ending put me off a bit. It will be interesting to see where this series goes next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9255346442295218327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3977500-chris?shelf=russian-stuff">russian-stuff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer138248011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7507360161737455496">These Russian translated books are a bit hard to get into at first because the culture and some of the language is so different, but once you get into the first 20 pgs or so, it's pretty addictive. This was the second book in the Nightwatch series and picks up a bit after the first one lets off. I wish I could give it 3.5 stars because I'm torn between liking it and REALLY liking it. The writing is excellent, the main characters are well developed and the plot twists are expert. The reader and O</span>
  <span id="freeText7507360161737455496" style="display:none">These Russian translated books are a bit hard to get into at first because the culture and some of the language is so different, but once you get into the first 20 pgs or so, it's pretty addictive. This was the second book in the Nightwatch series and picks up a bit after the first one lets off. I wish I could give it 3.5 stars because I'm torn between liking it and REALLY liking it. The writing is excellent, the main characters are well developed and the plot twists are expert. The reader and Others on the watches are expecting one thing but then some master plan unravels that the big wigs have known about all along and you're just as blind-sided by it as most of the characters. Anton is one of the best characters because he doesn't buy into Destiny quite as much as the others and is always actively trying to circumvent the negative things that are going on. He's a Light Other, but not entirely. He's worked with the head of the Dark Others a few times and I frequently get the sense that he's just on the cusp of figuring out the big picture and surpassing the trivialities of Light v. Dark. He's starting to see the pointlessness of it and how there is no real difference between the two but he isn't quite there yet because he's still stuck in the Light's blind hatred of the Dark. <br />One thing I find in these books that seems a relevant comment on the human race is the blind hatred the two sides (Light v Dark) have for each other. There's an ever-raging war and either side is only vaguely aware of why, it's just been going on so long that there is no real question of it; it has always been. (RE: Israel v. Palestine, Muslims v Christians v Jews) There are several of these battles going on now in the world and no one really seems to question much of the reasoning. Most participants are content to just go on hating and fighting without much reason. To me, that seems to be the main commentary brought to mind by these Nightwatch books. And with Daywatch, there is a hint of the beginnings of the possibility for love to conquer hate. I liked that about this book.<br /><br />***SPOILER***<br />I also don't quite know what to believe about Svetlana. At the end, it gets revealed that she is to be the mother of a female Messiah, the next coming of Jesus. I still don't know what to think about that. But, since it came about largely because of Gesar fooling with her destiny, I'm not likely to accept it until it actually happens. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7507360161737455496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_537202240" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537202240" />
    <a title="Seph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7747386-seph"><img alt="Seph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384904016p2/7747386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537202240?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seph" href="/user/show/7747386-seph">Seph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537202240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9003851256487127671">Sergei Lukyanenko's "Watch" hexology is a sleek urban-fantasy that simultaneously interweaves threats of an apocalyptic caliber with complex philosophical musings on human nature, to create an artful exploration of the relationship between good and evil, as witnessed through the eyes of a protagonist with an ever-changing scale of morality. All six volumes in the series have been beautifully translated from their native Russian into English by Andrew Bromfield.<br/><br/>Volume 2, Day Watch: introduces us,</span>
  <span id="freeText9003851256487127671" style="display:none">Sergei Lukyanenko's "Watch" hexology is a sleek urban-fantasy that simultaneously interweaves threats of an apocalyptic caliber with complex philosophical musings on human nature, to create an artful exploration of the relationship between good and evil, as witnessed through the eyes of a protagonist with an ever-changing scale of morality. All six volumes in the series have been beautifully translated from their native Russian into English by Andrew Bromfield.<br /><br />Volume 2, Day Watch: introduces us, formally, to The Inquisition, a "third power" among Others established to oversee the global activities of both Watches. The Inquisition is composed of both the Light and Dark Others whose auras have become neutral, allowing them to judge the actions of Light and Dark others indiscriminately and without bias. Ramifications from the events of "Night Watch" are also revealed: Anton and Svetlana have married; Olga has been fully restored to her human form; and the Chalk of Fate was successfully used on the Book of Destiny to alter the fate of Svetlana, permitting her to have an Absolute Other daughter, a Light Enchantress beyond classification.<br /><br />"Day Watch" is told from the perspective of three Dark Others: Alisa Donnikova, a third-degree Dark Witch who temporarily loses her power to use magic and falls in love with a Light Other while regaining it; Vitaly Rogoza, a Dark Mirror Magician---an Other capable of instantaneously matching the magical level of any Other he encounters---who visits Moscow to restore the balance of power between Light and Dark others; and Edgar, a third-degree Dark Magician who inadvertently becomes embroiled in a plot by Zabulon---head of the Moscow Day Watch---to potentially resurrect a Dark Magician Beyond Classification in order to begin the Apocalypse. The second volume also includes more narration from Anton Gorodetsky, whose involvement with each of the Dark Others reveals that all may not be as it seems, and that the obvious dangers are not always the most important.<br /><br />Additional secondary characters are introduced in Volume 2, including Witezslav, a Higher Vampire and one of The Inquisition's strongest acting members; Igor, a third-degree Light Magician who falls in love with Alisa while also recovering his depleted ability to use magic; and the Regin Brothers, a cult of Dark Others determined to resurrect their leader, the ancient Dark Dragon-Mage Fafnir, whose presence could signal the Apocalypse.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9003851256487127671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

His works often feature intense action-packed plots, interwoven with the moral dilemma of keeping one's humanity while being strong.<br /><br />Lukyanenko is a prolific writer, releasing usually 1-2 books per year, as well as a number of a critical articles and short stories. Recently his works have been adapted into film productions, for which he wrote the screenplays. He lives in Moscow with his wife Sonia and two sons, Artemiy and Danil, keeps mice as pets and enjoys cooking.<br /></span>
